<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman">&#9679;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:ARIAL; font-size:10.5pt"><B>Company updates full-year fiscal 2024 outlook to reflect expectations for slower volume recovery and greater Holistic
Margin Management (HMM) cost savings</B> </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:14pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:ARIAL"><I>&sup1; Please see Note 7 to the Consolidated Financial Statements below for reconciliation of this
and other <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measures used in this release. </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:14pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:5%; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL">MINNEAPOLIS (Dec. 20, 2023) &#150; General Mills,
Inc. (NYSE: GIS) today reported results for its fiscal 2024 second quarter. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:14pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:5%; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL">&#147;While we saw a slower-than-expected volume recovery in the
second quarter amid a continued challenging consumer landscape, we generated bottom-line growth thanks primarily to strong HMM cost savings,&#148; said General Mills Chairman and Chief Executive Officer Jeff Harmening. &#147;We&#146;re adapting our
plans to the evolving consumer environment and staying focused on driving long-term growth, with a priority on winning through innovation, brand building, and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">in-store</FONT> execution. At the same time, we&#146;re
stepping up our HMM performance and further eliminating disruption-related costs in the supply chain. For the full year, we&#146;ve revised our topline outlook to account for a slower volume recovery, narrowed our profit and EPS expectations within
our original guidance ranges, and maintained our outlook for strong free cash flow conversion.&#148; </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:14pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:5%; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL">General Mills is executing its Accelerate
strategy to drive sustainable, profitable growth and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">top-tier</FONT> shareholder returns over the long term. The strategy focuses on four pillars to create competitive advantages and win: boldly building brands,
relentlessly innovating, unleashing scale, and standing for good. The company is prioritizing its core markets, global platforms, and local gem brands that have the best prospects for profitable growth and is committed to reshaping its portfolio
with strategic acquisitions and divestitures to further enhance its growth profile. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL"><B><U>Second Quarter Results Summary </U></B></P>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:ARIAL; font-size:10.5pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:ARIAL; font-size:10.5pt"><B>Net sales</B> were down 2&nbsp;percent to $5.1&nbsp;billion, with lower pound volume partially offset by favorable net
price realization and mix. Organic net sales were 2&nbsp;percent below <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">year-ago</FONT> results that grew double digits; organic net sales were up 4&nbsp;percent on a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT>
compound growth basis. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:ARIAL; font-size:10.5pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

net price realization and mix, partially offset by input cost inflation, higher other supply chain costs, and supply </P></TD></TR></TABLE>

offset by input cost inflation, higher other supply chain costs, and supply chain deleverage. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:ARIAL; font-size:10.5pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:ARIAL; font-size:10.5pt"><B>Operating profit </B>of $812&nbsp;million was up 2&nbsp;percent, driven by higher gross profit dollars and lower
compensation and benefits expenses, partially offset by a goodwill impairment charge related to the Latin America reporting unit. <B>Operating profit margin</B> of 15.8&nbsp;percent was up 50 basis points. Adjusted operating profit of
$989&nbsp;million increased 13&nbsp;percent in constant currency, driven by higher adjusted gross profit dollars and lower compensation and benefits expenses. Adjusted operating profit margin was up 240 basis points to 19.3&nbsp;percent.
</P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:ARIAL; font-size:10.5pt"><B>Net earnings attributable to General Mills</B> of $596&nbsp;million were down 2&nbsp;percent. <B>Diluted EPS</B> was
up 1&nbsp;percent to $1.02, driven primarily by higher operating profit and lower net shares outstanding, partially offset by higher net interest expense. Adjusted diluted EPS of $1.25 was up 14&nbsp;percent in constant currency, driven primarily by
higher adjusted operating profit and lower net shares outstanding, partially offset by higher net interest expense. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL"><B><U>Six Month Results
Summary </U></B></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:ARIAL; font-size:10.5pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:ARIAL; font-size:10.5pt"><B>Net sales</B> increased 1&nbsp;percent to $10.0&nbsp;billion, driven by favorable net price realization and mix,
partially offset by lower pound volume. Organic net sales were 1&nbsp;percent above <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">year-ago</FONT> results that grew double digits; organic net sales were up 6&nbsp;percent on a
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT> compound growth basis. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:ARIAL; font-size:10.5pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:ARIAL; font-size:10.5pt"><B>Gross margin</B> was up 350 basis points to 35.2&nbsp;percent of net sales, driven by favorable net price realization
and mix, HMM cost savings, and favorable <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> effects, partially offset by input cost inflation, higher other supply chain costs, and supply chain deleverage.
Adjusted gross margin was up 120 basis points to 35.2&nbsp;percent of net sales, driven by favorable net price realization and mix and HMM cost savings, partially offset by input cost inflation, higher other supply chain costs, and supply chain
deleverage. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:ARIAL; font-size:10.5pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:ARIAL; font-size:10.5pt"><B>Operating profit </B>of $1.7&nbsp;billion was down 8&nbsp;percent, driven primarily by net gains on divestitures in
the prior year and a goodwill impairment charge related to the Latin America reporting unit, partially offset by higher gross profit dollars.<B> Operating profit margin</B> of 17.3&nbsp;percent was down 170 basis points. Adjusted operating profit of
$1.9&nbsp;billion increased 7&nbsp;percent in constant currency, driven by higher adjusted gross profit dollars, partially offset by higher adjusted selling, general, and administrative (SG&amp;A) expenses, including a high-single-digit increase in
media investment. Adjusted operating profit margin was up 110 basis points to 18.8&nbsp;percent. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:ARIAL; font-size:10.5pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:ARIAL; font-size:10.5pt"><B>Net earnings attributable to General Mills</B> were down 11&nbsp;percent to $1.3&nbsp;billion and <B>diluted EPS</B>
was down 8&nbsp;percent to $2.16, driven primarily by lower operating profit and higher net interest expense, partially offset by lower net shares outstanding. Adjusted diluted EPS of $2.34 was up 6&nbsp;percent in constant currency, driven
primarily by higher adjusted operating profit and lower net shares outstanding, partially offset by higher net interest expense and a higher adjusted effective tax rate. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL"><U>Notes on Comparability </U></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:4pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL">The following transactions impacted the
comparability of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">year-to-date</FONT></FONT> financial results between fiscal 2023 and fiscal 2024: the acquisition of the TNT Crust foodservice business in the first quarter of fiscal
2023 and the divestiture of the Helper main meals and Suddenly Salad side dishes business in the first quarter of fiscal 2023. In addition, results in the first half of fiscal 2023 included the impact of a voluntary recall on certain international
<I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">H&auml;agen-Dazs</FONT></I> ice cream products, which was a headwind to net sales and operating profit results in the International segment. </P>
</DIV></Center>

<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always"> </p>
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL"><U>North America Retail Segment </U></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:4pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL">Second-quarter net sales for General Mills&#146; North America Retail segment were down 2&nbsp;percent to $3.3&nbsp;billion, driven by lower pound volume, partially
offset by favorable net price realization and mix. Organic net sales were 2&nbsp;percent below <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">year-ago</FONT> results that grew double digits; organic net sales were up 5&nbsp;percent on a <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT> compound growth basis. Net sales performance outpaced Nielsen-measured retail sales growth in the quarter due to faster growth in <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-measured</FONT> channels. Net sales were
down <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mid-single</FONT> digits for the U.S. Snacks and U.S. Morning Foods operating units. Net sales were up <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">low-single</FONT> digits for U.S. Meals&nbsp;&amp; Baking Solutions and
were up high-single digits for Canada. Segment operating profit of $860&nbsp;million was up 3&nbsp;percent as reported and in constant currency, driven primarily by favorable net price realization and mix and HMM cost savings, partially offset by
lower volume, input cost inflation, higher other supply chain costs, supply chain deleverage, and higher SG&amp;A expenses. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:5%; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL">Through six months,
North America Retail segment net sales of $6.4&nbsp;billion essentially matched <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">year-ago</FONT> levels, including a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">1-point</FONT> headwind from divestitures. Organic net sales were
up 1&nbsp;percent. Segment operating profit of $1.7&nbsp;billion was up 3&nbsp;percent as reported and in constant currency, driven primarily by favorable net price realization and mix and HMM cost savings, partially offset by input cost inflation,
lower volume, higher other supply chain costs, higher SG&amp;A expenses, and supply chain deleverage. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL"><U>Pet Segment </U></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:4pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL">Second-quarter net sales for the Pet segment were down 4&nbsp;percent to $569&nbsp;million, driven by lower pound volume, partially offset by favorable net price
realization and mix. Organic net sales were also down 4&nbsp;percent. Net sales performance lagged <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">all-channel</FONT> retail sales results by roughly 2 points, despite the comparison to the <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">year-ago</FONT> quarter that included a significant retailer inventory reduction. Relative to fiscal 2022, second-quarter net sales were down <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mid-single</FONT> digits and <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">all-channel</FONT> retail sales were up <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mid-single</FONT> digits. Net sales in the quarter were down <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mid-single</FONT> digits for dry pet food, down double
digits for wet pet food, and up double digits for pet treats compared to the prior year. Segment operating profit of $102&nbsp;million was up 18&nbsp;percent, driven primarily by favorable net price realization and mix and HMM cost savings,
partially offset by lower volume, higher other supply chain costs, and higher SG&amp;A expenses. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:5%; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL">Through six months, Pet segment net sales were
down 2&nbsp;percent to $1.1&nbsp;billion. Organic net sales were also down 2&nbsp;percent. Segment operating profit was up 2&nbsp;percent to $214&nbsp;million, driven primarily by favorable net price realization and mix and HMM cost savings,
partially offset by higher other supply chain costs, lower volume, input cost inflation, higher SG&amp;A expenses, and supply chain deleverage. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL"><U>North America
Foodservice Segment </U></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:4pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL">Second-quarter net sales for the North America Foodservice segment essentially matched <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">year-ago</FONT>
levels at $582&nbsp;million. Organic net sales were in line with last year despite a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-point</FONT> headwind from market index pricing on bakery flour. Segment operating profit increased 17&nbsp;percent to
$96&nbsp;million, driven primarily by HMM cost savings and favorable net price realization and mix, partially offset by higher other supply chain costs. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:5%; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL">Through six months, North America Foodservice net sales increased 4&nbsp;percent to $1.1&nbsp;billion, including a
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-point</FONT> benefit from the TNT Crust acquisition. Organic net sales were up 2&nbsp;percent. Segment operating profit was up 14&nbsp;percent to $155&nbsp;million, driven by favorable net price realization and mix
and HMM cost savings, partially offset by higher other supply chain costs and higher SG&amp;A expenses. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL"><U>International Segment </U></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:4pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL">Second-quarter net sales for the International segment increased 2&nbsp;percent to $683&nbsp;million, driven by favorable net price realization and mix and a <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-point</FONT> benefit from foreign currency exchange, partially offset by lower pound volume. Organic net sales essentially matched <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">year-ago</FONT> levels, with a decline in Brazil offset
by growth in distributor markets and Europe&nbsp;&amp; Australia. Segment operating profit of $35&nbsp;million was up 94&nbsp;percent as reported and up 100&nbsp;percent in constant currency from <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">year-ago</FONT>
results that included the impact of the ice cream recall, driven by favorable net price realization and mix and HMM cost savings, partially offset by input cost inflation. </P>
</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always"> </p>
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:5%; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL">Through six months, International net sales increased 6&nbsp;percent to $1.4&nbsp;billion, including
a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-point</FONT> benefit from foreign currency exchange. Organic net sales were up 4&nbsp;percent. Segment operating profit of $85&nbsp;million was up 61&nbsp;percent as reported and up 68&nbsp;percent in constant
currency from <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">year-ago</FONT> results that included the impact of the ice cream recall, driven by favorable net price realization and mix and HMM cost savings, partially offset by input cost inflation and lower
volume. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL"><B><U>Joint Venture Summary </U></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:4pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL">Second-quarter
constant-currency net sales increased 11&nbsp;percent for Cereal Partners Worldwide (CPW), driven by favorable net price realization and mix, partially offset by lower pound volume. Constant-currency net sales for
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">H&auml;agen-Dazs</FONT> Japan (HDJ) were up 6&nbsp;percent, driven by favorable net price realization and mix, partially offset by lower pound volume. Combined <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">after-tax</FONT>
earnings from joint ventures of $24&nbsp;million were down 5&nbsp;percent, driven by unfavorable foreign currency exchange, partially offset by constant-currency <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">after-tax</FONT> earnings growth for HDJ. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL"><B><U>Other Income Statement Items </U></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:4pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL">Second-quarter unallocated corporate
items totaled $157&nbsp;million net expense in fiscal 2024 compared to $212&nbsp;million net expense a year ago. Excluding <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> valuation effects and other
items affecting comparability, unallocated corporate items totaled $103&nbsp;million net expense this year compared to $142&nbsp;million net expense last year, driven primarily by lower compensation and benefits expenses. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:5%; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL">Restructuring, impairment, and other exit costs totaled $124&nbsp;million in the second quarter compared to $11&nbsp;million a year ago <I>(please see
Note 3 below for more information on these charges)</I>. Benefit plan <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-service</FONT> income totaled $20&nbsp;million in the second quarter compared to $22&nbsp;million a year ago, driven primarily by an increase
in interest costs, partially offset by lower amortization of losses and higher expected return on plan assets. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:5%; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL">Net interest expense totaled
$118&nbsp;million in the second quarter compared to $92&nbsp;million a year ago, driven primarily by higher interest rates and higher average long-term debt levels. The effective tax rate in the quarter was 19.0&nbsp;percent compared to
20.2&nbsp;percent last year <I>(please see Note 6 below for more information on our effective tax rate)</I>. The second-quarter adjusted effective tax rate was 20.8&nbsp;percent compared to 21.1&nbsp;percent a year ago, driven primarily by favorable
earnings mix by jurisdiction in fiscal 2024. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL"><B><U>Cash Flow Generation and Cash Returns </U></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:4pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL">Cash provided by operating activities totaled $1.5&nbsp;billion through six months of fiscal 2024 compared to $1.2&nbsp;billion a year ago. Capital investments totaled
$294&nbsp;million compared to $227&nbsp;million a year ago. Dividends paid increased 7&nbsp;percent to $691&nbsp;million. General Mills repurchased approximately 18.8&nbsp;million shares of common stock through six months of fiscal 2024 for a total
of $1.3&nbsp;billion compared to $901&nbsp;million in share repurchases a year ago. Average diluted shares outstanding in the first half decreased 3&nbsp;percent to 587&nbsp;million. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL"><B><U>Fiscal 2024 Outlook </U></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:4pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL">General Mills continues to expect the largest
factors impacting its performance in fiscal 2024 will be the economic health of consumers, the moderating rate of input cost inflation, and the increasing stability of the supply chain environment. Relative to its previous expectation, the company
now expects a slower volume recovery in fiscal 2024, reflecting a more cautious consumer economic outlook and a faster normalization of competitive <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">on-shelf</FONT> availability. For the full year, the company
continues to expect input cost inflation of approximately 5&nbsp;percent of total cost of goods sold, driven primarily by labor inflation that impacts sourcing, manufacturing, and logistics costs. The company now expects to generate Holistic Margin
Management (HMM) cost savings of roughly 5&nbsp;percent of cost of goods sold in fiscal 2024, up from its previous expectation of 4&nbsp;percent and higher than the 3&nbsp;percent achieved in fiscal 2023. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10.5pt; font-family:ARIAL">Based on the above assumptions, the company updated its full-year fiscal 2024 financial targets&sup2;: </P>
</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always"> </p>

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">

<TD WIDTH="3%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman">&#9679;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:ARIAL; font-size:10.5pt"><B>Organic net sales</B> are now expected to range between down 1&nbsp;percent and flat, compared to the previous range
of 3 to 4&nbsp;percent growth, reflecting a slower volume recovery in fiscal 2024. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:2pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:ARIAL; font-size:10.5pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman">&#9679;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:ARIAL; font-size:10.5pt"><B>Adjusted operating profit</B> and <B>adjusted diluted EPS</B> are now expected to increase 4 to 5&nbsp;percent in
constant currency, compared to the previous range of 4 to 6&nbsp;percent growth in constant currency, reflecting the impact of lower organic sales growth, largely offset by higher HMM cost savings and greater elimination of disruption-related costs
in the supply chain. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:2pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:ARIAL; font-size:10.5pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">

markets for our products, including new product introductions, advertising activities, pricing actions, and promotional activities of our competitors; economic conditions, including changes in inflation rates, interest rates, tax rates, or the
availability of capital; product development and innovation; consumer acceptance of new products and product improvements; consumer reaction to pricing actions and changes in promotion levels; acquisitions or dispositions of businesses or assets;
changes in capital structure; changes in the legal and regulatory environment, including tax legislation, labeling and advertising regulations, and litigation; impairments in the carrying value of goodwill, other intangible assets, or other
long-lived assets, or changes in the useful lives of other intangible assets; changes in accounting standards and the impact of significant accounting estimates; product quality and safety issues, including recalls and product liability; changes in
consumer demand for our products; effectiveness of advertising, marketing, and promotional programs; changes in consumer behavior, trends, and preferences, including weight loss trends; consumer perception of health-related issues, including
obesity; consolidation in the retail environment; changes in purchasing and inventory levels of significant customers; fluctuations in the cost and availability of supply chain resources, including raw materials, packaging, energy, and
transportation; effectiveness of restructuring and cost saving initiatives; volatility in the market value of derivatives used to manage price risk for certain commodities; benefit plan expenses due to changes in plan asset values and discount rates
used to determine plan liabilities; failure or breach of our information technology systems; foreign economic conditions, including currency rate fluctuations; and political unrest in foreign markets and economic uncertainty due to terrorism or war.

second quarter of fiscal 2024, we approved a restructuring action to enhance the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">go-to-market</FONT></FONT> commercial strategy and associated organizational structure of our Pet
segment. We expect to incur approximately $22&nbsp;million of restructuring charges and project-related expenses related to this action, of which approximately $4&nbsp;million will be cash. These charges are expected to consist of approximately
$16&nbsp;million of accelerated depreciation and $6&nbsp;million of other costs, including severance. We recognized $2&nbsp;million of accelerated depreciation and $3&nbsp;million of other costs, including severance, in the <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">six-month</FONT> period ended November&nbsp;26, 2023. We expect this action to be completed by the end of fiscal 2026. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:10pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:3%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">We recorded $10&nbsp;million of restructuring charges in the second quarter of fiscal 2024 and $20&nbsp;million of
restructuring charges in the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">six-month</FONT> period ended November&nbsp;26, 2023, related to restructuring actions previously announced. We recorded $12&nbsp;million of restructuring charges in the second quarter of
fiscal 2023 and $14&nbsp;million of restructuring charges in the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">six-month</FONT> period ended November&nbsp;27, 2022, related to restructuring actions previously announced. We expect these actions to be completed by
the end of fiscal 2025. </P>

<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always"> </p>
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">

<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(4)</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="justify">Unallocated corporate expenses totaled $157&nbsp;million in the second quarter of fiscal 2024, compared to
$212&nbsp;million in the same period in fiscal 2023. In the second quarter of fiscal 2024, we recorded a $25&nbsp;million net increase in expense related to the
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> valuation of certain commodity positions and grain inventories, compared to a $25&nbsp;million net increase in expense in the same period last year. We
recorded $20&nbsp;million of net losses related to valuation adjustments on certain corporate investments in the second&nbsp;quarter of fiscal 2024, compared to $36&nbsp;million of net losses related to valuation adjustments and the loss on sale of
certain corporate investments in the second quarter of fiscal 2023. We recorded $8&nbsp;million of restructuring charges in the second&nbsp;quarter of fiscal 2024. In the second quarter of fiscal 2023, we recorded a $3&nbsp;million charge related to
a voluntary recall on certain international <I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">H&auml;agen-Dazs</FONT></I> ice cream products. In addition, we recorded $3&nbsp;million of integration costs primarily related to our acquisition of TNT Crust and
$2&nbsp;million of transaction costs primarily related to the sale of our Helper main meals and Suddenly Salad side dishes business in the second quarter of fiscal 2023. Certain compensation and benefits expenses decreased in the second quarter of
fiscal 2024, compared to the same period last year. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:10pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:3%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">Unallocated corporate expenses totaled
$244&nbsp;million in the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">six-month</FONT> period ended November&nbsp;26, 2023, compared to $545&nbsp;million in the same period last year. We recorded a $20&nbsp;million net decrease in expense related to the <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> valuation of certain commodity positions and grain inventories in the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">six-month</FONT> period ended November&nbsp;26, 2023,
compared to a $200&nbsp;million net increase in expense in the same period last year. We recorded $22&nbsp;million of net losses related to valuation adjustments and the sale of corporate investments in the
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">six-month</FONT> period ended November&nbsp;26, 2023, compared to $62&nbsp;million of net losses in the same period last year. In the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">six-month</FONT> period ended November&nbsp;27,
2022, we recorded a $24&nbsp;million charge related to a voluntary recall on certain international <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">H&auml;agen-Dazs</FONT> ice cream products. We recorded $17&nbsp;million of restructuring charges and $1&nbsp;million
of restructuring initiative project-related costs in cost of sales in the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">six-month</FONT> period ended November&nbsp;26, 2023, compared to $1&nbsp;million of restructuring charges in cost of sales in the same period
last year. In addition, we recorded $4&nbsp;million of integration costs primarily related to our acquisition of TNT Crust and $2&nbsp;million of transaction costs primarily related to the sale of our Helper main meals and Suddenly Salad side dishes
business in the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">six-month</FONT> period ended November&nbsp;27, 2022. Certain compensation and benefits expenses decreased in the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">six-month</FONT> period ended November&nbsp;26, 2023,
compared to the same period last year. </P> <P STYLE="font-size:10pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="justify">The effective tax rate for the second quarter of fiscal 2024 was 19.0&nbsp;percent compared to
20.2&nbsp;percent for the second quarter of fiscal 2023. The 1.2 percentage point decrease was primarily due to favorable changes in earnings mix by jurisdiction and certain nonrecurring discrete tax benefits in the second quarter of fiscal 2024.
Our effective tax rate excluding certain items affecting comparability was 20.8&nbsp;percent in the second quarter of fiscal 2024, compared to 21.1&nbsp;percent in the same period last year (see Note 7 below for a description of our use of measures
not defined by GAAP). The 0.3 percentage point decrease was primarily due to favorable earnings mix by jurisdiction in the second quarter of fiscal 2024. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="margin-top:10pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:3%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">The effective tax rate for the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">six-month</FONT> period ended November&nbsp;26, 2023, was
20.0&nbsp;percent compared to 20.8&nbsp;percent for the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">six-month</FONT> period ended November&nbsp;27, 2022. The 0.8 percentage point decrease was primarily due to unfavorable tax components related to the
divestitures in fiscal 2023 and favorable earnings mix by jurisdiction in fiscal 2024, partially offset by certain nonrecurring discrete tax benefits in fiscal 2023. Our effective tax rate excluding certain items affecting comparability was
21.0&nbsp;percent in the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">six-month</FONT> period ended November&nbsp;26, 2023, compared to 20.4&nbsp;percent in the same period last year (see Note 7 below for a description of our use of measures not defined by
GAAP). The 0.6 percentage point increase was primarily due to certain nonrecurring discrete tax benefits in fiscal 2023. </P> <P STYLE="font-size:10pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="justify">We have included measures in this release that are not defined by GAAP. We believe that these measures
provide useful information to investors, and include these measures in other communications to investors. For each of these <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures, we are providing below a reconciliation of the
differences between the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measure and the most directly comparable GAAP measure, an explanation of why we believe the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measure provides useful information
to investors and any additional material purposes for which our management or Board of Directors uses the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measure. These <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measures should be viewed in
addition to, and not in lieu of, the comparable GAAP measure. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>

<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always"> </p>
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:3%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">We provide organic net sales growth rates for our consolidated net sales and
segment net sales. This measure is used in reporting to our Board of Directors and executive management and as a component of the Board of Directors&#146; measurement of our performance for incentive compensation purposes. We believe that organic
net sales growth rates provide useful information to investors because they provide transparency to underlying performance in our net sales by excluding the effect that foreign currency exchange rate fluctuations, acquisitions, divestitures, and a
53rd&nbsp;fiscal week, when applicable, have on <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">year-to-year</FONT></FONT> comparability. A reconciliation of these measures to reported net sales growth rates, the relevant GAAP
measures, are included in our Operating Segment Results above. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:10pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:3%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">Certain measures in this release are presented excluding
the impact of foreign currency exchange (constant-currency). To present this information, current period results for entities reporting in currencies other than United States dollars are translated into United States dollars at the average exchange
rates in effect during the corresponding period of the prior fiscal year, rather than the actual average exchange rates in effect during the current fiscal year. Therefore, the foreign currency impact is equal to current year results in local
currencies multiplied by the change in the average foreign currency exchange rate between the current fiscal period and the corresponding period of the prior fiscal year. We believe that these constant-currency measures provide useful information to
investors because they provide transparency to underlying performance by excluding the effect that foreign currency exchange rate fluctuations have on <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">period-to-period</FONT></FONT>
comparability given volatility in foreign currency exchange markets. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:10pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:3%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">Our fiscal 2024 outlook for organic net sales
growth, adjusted operating profit growth, adjusted diluted EPS growth, and free cash flow conversion are <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures that exclude, or have otherwise been adjusted for, items impacting
comparability, including the effect of foreign currency exchange rate fluctuations, acquisitions, divestitures, and a 53rd week, when applicable. We are not able to reconcile these forward-looking <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT>
financial measures to their most directly comparable forward-looking GAAP financial measure without unreasonable efforts because we are unable to predict with a reasonable degree of certainty the actual impact of changes in foreign currency exchange
rates or the timing of acquisitions and divestitures throughout fiscal 2024. The unavailable information could have a significant impact on our fiscal 2024 GAAP financial results. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:10pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:3%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">For fiscal 2024, we currently expect: foreign currency exchange rates (based on a blend of forward and forecasted rates and
hedge positions) and acquisitions and divestitures will have no material impact to net sales growth and restructuring charges to total approximately $45&nbsp;million to $50&nbsp;million. </P>
</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always"> </p>
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Significant Items Impacting Comparability </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:10pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">Several measures below are presented on an adjusted basis. The adjustments are either items resulting from infrequently occurring events or
items that, in management&#146;s judgement, significantly affect the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">year-to-year</FONT></FONT> assessment of operating results. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:10pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">The following are descriptions of significant items impacting comparability of our results. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:10pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:7%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Goodwill impairment </U></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:7%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-cash</FONT> goodwill impairment charge related to our Latin America reporting unit. Please
see Note&nbsp;3. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:10pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:7%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Restructuring charges and project-related costs </U></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:7%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">Restructuring charges and project-related costs related to a commercial strategy restructuring action and previously announced
restructuring actions recorded in fiscal 2024. Restructuring charges for previously announced restructuring actions recorded in fiscal 2023. Please see Note&nbsp;3. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:10pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:7%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Investment activity, net </U></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:7%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">Valuation adjustments of certain corporate investments in fiscal 2024. Valuation adjustments and the loss on sale of certain
corporate investments in fiscal 2023. Please see Note&nbsp;4. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:10pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:7%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> effects </U></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:7%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">Net <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> valuation of certain
commodity positions recognized in unallocated corporate items. Please see Note&nbsp;4. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:10pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:7%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Transaction costs </U></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:7%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">Immaterial transaction costs incurred in fiscal 2024. Transaction costs primarily related to the sale of our Helper main meals
and Suddenly Salad side dishes business in fiscal 2023. Please see Note&nbsp;2. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:10pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:7%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Product recall </U></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:7%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">Costs related to the fiscal 2023 voluntary recall of certain international
<I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">H&auml;agen-Dazs</FONT></I> ice cream products. Please see Note&nbsp;4. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:10pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:7%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Acquisition integration
costs </U></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:7%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">Integration costs primarily resulting from the acquisition of TNT Crust in fiscal 2024 and fiscal 2023. Please
see Note&nbsp;2. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:10pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:7%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Divestitures gain, net </U></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:7%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">Net divestitures gain primarily related to the sale of our Helper main meals and Suddenly Salad side dishes business in fiscal
2023. Please see Note&nbsp;2. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:10pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:7%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>CPW restructuring charges </U></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:7%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">CPW restructuring charges related to previously announced restructuring actions. </P>

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Adjusted Operating Profit Growth on a Constant-currency Basis </U></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:10pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">This measure is used in reporting to our Board of Directors and executive management and as a component of the measurement of our performance
for incentive compensation purposes. We believe that this measure provides useful information to investors because it is the operating profit measure we use to evaluate operating profit performance on a comparable <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">year-to-year</FONT></FONT> basis. The measure is evaluated on a constant-currency basis by excluding the effect that foreign currency exchange rate fluctuations have on <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">year-to-year</FONT></FONT> comparability given the volatility in foreign currency exchange rates. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:10pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">Our adjusted
operating profit growth on a constant-currency basis is calculated as follows: </P> <P STYLE="font-size:10pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Constant-currency Segment Operating Profit Growth Rates </U></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">We believe that this measure provides useful information to investors because it provides transparency to underlying performance of our
segments by excluding the effect that foreign currency exchange rate fluctuations have on <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">year-to-year</FONT></FONT> comparability given volatility in foreign currency exchange
markets. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">Our segments&#146; operating profit growth rates on a constant-currency basis are calculated as follows: </P>
<P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE CELLSPACING="0" CELLPADDING="0" WIDTH="100%" BORDER="0" STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" ALIGN="center">


<TR>

<P STYLE="margin-top:24pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Net Sales Growth Rates for our Canada Operating Unit on a Constant-currency Basis </U></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">We believe that this measure of our Canada operating unit net sales provides useful information to investors because it provides transparency
to underlying performance of our Canada operating unit within our North America Retail segment by excluding the effect that foreign currency exchange rate fluctuations have on
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">year-to-year</FONT></FONT> comparability given volatility in foreign currency exchange markets. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:9.5pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">Net sales growth rates for our Canada operating unit on a constant-currency basis are calculated as follows: </P>
<P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Adjusted Effective Income Tax Rate </U></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">We believe this measure provides useful information to investors because it presents the adjusted effective income tax rate on a comparable <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">year-to-year</FONT></FONT> basis. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">Adjusted effective income tax rates are
calculated as follows: </P> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
